###xml 1766 1769 1576 1579 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">max</sub>
###xml 1911 1912 1706 1707 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 2046 2047 1830 1831 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 2136 2137 1912 1913 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">F</bold>
###xml 2279 2280 2048 2049 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 2316 2317 2081 2082 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sub>
###xml 2329 2330 2091 2092 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 2398 2399 2157 2158 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 2404 2405 2160 2161 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 2429 2430 2182 2183 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
Interactions of the beta clamp with the delta subunit of DnaX. (A) Representative SPR results analyzing interaction of delta (4 muM) with various beta clamp proteins (approximately100 RU). Clamps examined include the his6-tagged beta+ homodimer (beta+), the his6-tagged betaC homodimer (betaC), the his6-tagged beta+/myc-tagged beta+ heterodimer (beta+/beta+) and the his6-tagged beta+/myc-tagged betaC heterodimer (beta+/betaC). Theoretical Rmax values for binding of a single delta subunit (delta1), or for two delta subunits (delta2) are indicated by dashed lines. (B) Titration of delta with his6-tagged beta+. Increasing concentrations of purified delta (0.1, 1, 10, 25, 50, 100, 250, 500, 750 and 1000 nM) were injected over approximately100 RU of his6-tagged beta+ captured on the anti-Penta*His chip surface. (C) Comparison of sensorgrams from low (25 nM) and high (1 microM) concentrations of delta injected over approximately100 RU of his6-tagged beta+ captured on the anti-Penta*His chip surface from panel (B) highlighting differences in association (ka) and dissociation rates (kd). The amplitudes (Rmax) of these SPR traces were normalized to each other to facilitate a direct comparison of the association and dissociation phases of the curves. (D) Titration of delta with beta+/betaC. Increasing concentrations of purified delta (10, 25, 50, 100 and 500 nM) were injected over approximately100 RU of beta+/betaC captured on the anti-Penta*His chip surface. (E) The double-injection experiment was performed as outlined in the cartoon (bottom). approximately100 RU of his6-tagged beta+ was captured on the anti-Penta*His chip surface (injection 1). Saturating levels (10 microM) of delta were injected (injection 2), forming the beta-delta2 complex (Rmax approaching 100 RU). Flow was switched to buffer, allowing for the more loosely bound delta (delta2) to dissociate, resulting in a beta-delta1 complex. Increasing concentrations of delta (0, 1, 10, 25, 50, 100, 250, 500, 750 and 1000 nM) were then injected over the beta-delta1 complex (injection 3) to determine the binding affinity for the second delta (delta2). (F) Summary table of kinetic constants for various clamp-delta interactions derived from SPR results summarized in (A-E). Results shown for beta+-delta were determined using the his6-tagged beta+ homodimer, and were indistinguishable from those observed with beta+/beta+. An interaction of betaC with delta was not detected (nd).
###end p 26
###begin p 27
###xml 101 102 90 91 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 206 207 171 172 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sub>
###xml 413 414 371 372 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 478 479 436 437 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sub>
###xml 761 762 715 716 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">R</italic>
###xml 762 765 716 719 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">max</sub>
###xml 1094 1095 1042 1043 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">k</italic>
###xml 1095 1096 1043 1044 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</sub>
###xml 1113 1114 1061 1062 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">k</italic>
###xml 1114 1115 1062 1063 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</sub>
###xml 1173 1174 1121 1122 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">k</italic>
###xml 1174 1175 1122 1123 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</sub>
###xml 1180 1181 1128 1129 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">k</italic>
###xml 1181 1182 1129 1130 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</sub>
###xml 1507 1508 1453 1454 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sup>
SPR experiments to determine kinetic values describing interactions of beta with delta or DnaX (gamma3deltadelta'chipsi) were conducted using an anti-Penta*His CM5 chip to capture approximately100 RU of his6-tagged clamp. The delta subunit, or DnaX, was injected at concentrations of 0.1-1000 nM, as noted. When analyzing beta-DnaX interactions, the running buffer lacked EDTA and was supplemented with 10 mM MgCl2 and 1 mM ATP. An anti-Penta*His C1 chip was used to capture his6-tagged clamps to characterize their interactions with Pol IIIalpha, which was injected at concentrations of 10-1000 nM. The values for all kinetic constants were obtained by fitting the SPR curves to the 1:1 Langmuir binding model provided with the BIAevaluation Software 4.1. The Rmax was changed from a global to a local parameter in all curve fits to account for slight variations in the amount of beta captured on the chip surface between regenerations. The equilibrium dissociation constants for beta binding to the DnaX complex in the presence of ATP were obtained using the steady state model. Both the on (ka) and off rates (kd) were too rapid to fit the curves using the simultaneous ka and kd 1:1 Langmuir binding model. Therefore, the off rates were determined by separately fitting only the dissociation portion of the binding curves. The on rates were then calculated using the following equation:  Each fit (with the exception of DnaX) was assessed by the numerical value for the sum of the squared residuals (chi2), which represents the sum of the deviations between the experimental data and the model to which it was fit.
###end p 27
###begin p 28
###xml 113 114 113 114 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">R</italic>
###xml 114 117 114 117 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">max</sub>
###xml 222 223 219 220 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">R</italic>
###xml 223 227 220 221 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</sub>
###xml 232 233 226 227 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</sub>
###xml 272 276 266 267 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</sub>
The stoichiometry (S) of partner interactions with the clamp was determined using the following equation:  where Rmax is the theoretical maximum response (RU) of binding to the clamp at a specific surface density of beta (Rbeta), MWA is the molecular weight of analyte, MWbeta is the molecular weight of tagged beta dimer (81.2 kDa as dimer), and S is the stoichiometry.
###end p 28
###begin title 29
ITC
###end title 29
###begin p 30
###xml 87 88 84 85 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 110 111 100 101 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 271 272 237 238 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
A VP-ITC microcalorimeter (MicroCal) was used to analyze interaction of myc-tagged beta+ with delta. Both beta+ and delta were dialyzed against HBS-EP Buffer, and then degassed at 37degreesC. delta (5.59 muM) was added to the cell pre-equilibrated to 37degreesC, and beta+ (55.9 muM as dimer) was the titrant. The stir speed was 307 r.p.m., the reference power was 20 mucal/s, and injections were 15 mul each at a rate of 0.5 mul/s, except for the first injection, which was at a rate of 1.0 mul/s. A control in which delta was present in the cell and buffer served as titrant was used for background subtraction. Kinetic values were obtained by fitting the binding isotherm to the sequential binding sites model using the Origin software, version 7.02b (Origin Lab Corporation), provided with the instrument.
###end p 30
###begin title 31
Clamp loading and unloading assays
###end title 31
###begin p 32
###xml 112 114 112 114 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B32">32</xref>
###xml 115 117 115 117 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B38">38</xref>
###xml 193 194 192 193 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 193 194 192 193 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><sup>&#8722;</sup></bold>
###xml 488 490 478 480 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
###xml 563 564 553 554 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sub>
###xml 765 767 752 754 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
Wild-type and mutant clamps were loaded onto a singly nicked, circular, dsDNA template as described previously (32,38). The nicked template was prepared by treatment of 50 mug of pBluescript SK- (Stratagene) with 500 U of Mung Bean nuclease (Promega) in the supplied Reaction Buffer at 2.5 x concentration for 30 min at 37degreesC. The DNA template was purified away from the reaction components using the QIAprep spin miniprep kit (Qiagen). Wild-type and mutant beta clamp proteins were 32P-labeled at the N-terminal cAMP-dependent kinase tag adjacent to the his6 tag using the catalytic subunit of cAMP-dependent protein kinase (New England Biolabs) according to manufacturer's instructions. In control reactions, the myc-tagged beta clamps were not labeled. The 32P-beta was purified away from unincorporated label using a His-SpinTrap column (GE Healthcare). Clamp was eluted from the column using 200 mul Buffer B containing 250 mM imidizole and adjusted to a final concentration of 1 muM (as dimer).
###end p 32
###begin p 33
###xml 15 16 11 12 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 124 126 102 104 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
###xml 150 151 122 123 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 157 158 126 127 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 166 167 132 133 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 172 173 135 136 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 273 274 235 236 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 670 672 618 620 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
###xml 856 858 801 803 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
The DnaX (gamma3deltadelta'chipsi) clamp loader complex (0.1 nM) was incubated for 10 min at 37degreesC with 250 nM of each 32P-beta clamp dimer (beta+, betaC or beta+/betaC) and 10 nM nicked pBluescript DNA in 100 mul of Loading Buffer [20 mM Tris-HCl (pH 7.5), 10 mM MgCl2, 5 mM DTT, 50 mug/ml BSA (Promega), 4% (v/v) glycerol, 125 mM NaCl and 1 mM ATP]. The loading reaction was then gel filtered through a 4 ml (packed bed volume; 0.5 cm x approximately20 cm) Sephacryl S-500 high-resolution media column (GE Healthcare) equilibrated in Loading Buffer containing 300 mM NaCl at room temperature. Fractions (250 mul) were collected manually, and fractions containing 32P-beta that was either loaded onto DNA or free was detected by liquid scintillation counting and native agarose gel electrophoresis (as described below). The peak fractions containing 32P-beta on DNA were quickly pooled to serve as substrate in clamp unloading assays.
###end p 33
###begin p 34
###xml 43 45 43 45 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
###xml 51 52 48 49 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 57 59 54 56 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
###xml 65 66 59 60 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 71 72 62 63 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 331 333 314 316 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
###xml 456 458 430 432 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
###xml 1013 1015 976 978 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
Clamp unloading assays were done using the 32P-beta+ and 32P-beta+/betaC clamps preloaded onto DNA, immediately after they were isolated by gel filtration. Reactions (20 mul) were initiated by adding either the DnaX clamp loader complex (10 nM to 5 muM) with 1 mM ATP, or the delta subunit (15 nM to 10 muM), to 10-mul aliquots of 32P-beta-DNA complex, followed by incubation at 37degreesC for 10 min. An aliquot of each unloading reaction, as well as the 32P-clamp-DNA substrate used (prior to addition of DnaX or delta), were mixed with 4 mul 6 x Sample Buffer (15% ficoll 400, 0.25% bromophenyl blue and 0.25% xylene cyanol) and loaded onto 1.5% native agarose gels cast in Running Buffer (90 mM Tris-base and 90 mM EDTA), and electrophoresed at 200 V for 140 min at room temperature. Gels were stained with ethidium bromide to detect DNA, photographed, fixed by incubation in 20% (v/v) acetic acid, dried on DEAE paper (Whatmann) at 80degreesC overnight and exposed using a phosphorimager screen to visualize 32P-beta.
###end p 34
###begin title 35
Primer extension assay
###end title 35
###begin p 36
###xml 19 20 16 17 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 26 27 20 21 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 35 36 26 27 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 41 42 29 30 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 115 117 103 105 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B21">21</xref>
###xml 215 216 202 203 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 315 316 302 303 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sup>
The ability of beta+, betaC or beta+/betaC to stimulate Pol III* replication was measured as described previously (21). Briefly, reactions (20 mul) containing Replication Buffer [20 mM Tris-HCl (pH 7.5), 8.0 mM MgCl2, 0.1 mM EDTA, 5 mM DTT, 1 mM ATP, 5% glycerol and 0.8 mg/ml BSA] were supplemented with 0.133 mM [3H-dTTP]-dNTPs (68.2 CPM/pmol), 2 muM ssDNA binding protein (SSB) and 5 nM of M13 ssDNA primed with SP20 (5'-ACGCCTGTAGCATTCCACAG-3'; Sigma Genosys). Reactions were initiated by addition of 1 nM Pol III*, and were quenched by addition of 1 ml of 15% trichloroacetic acid. Acid insoluble products were collected on 2.4-cm glass microfiber filters (VWR) by vacuum suction, and nucleotide incorporation was quantitated by liquid scintillation spectroscopy.
###end p 36
###begin title 37
RESULTS
###end title 37
###begin title 38
Generation of a beta clamp hydrophobic cleft mutant
###end title 38
###begin p 39
###xml 111 118 101 108 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">monomer</sub>
###xml 223 225 209 211 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B39">39</xref>
###xml 380 382 359 361 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B33">33</xref>
###xml 599 607 578 586 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 658 659 631 632 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 661 670 634 643 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">In silico</italic>
###xml 687 688 657 658 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 733 740 703 710 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 1137 1146 1104 1113 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in silico</italic>
###xml 1170 1171 1134 1135 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 1218 1226 1182 1190 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 1271 1272 1232 1233 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1309 1317 1270 1278 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 1359 1360 1317 1318 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 1467 1468 1412 1413 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 1532 1540 1473 1481 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 1648 1649 1582 1583 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1766 1767 1693 1694 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1804 1805 1724 1725 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 2015 2017 1927 1929 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B40">40</xref>
###xml 2028 2029 1937 1938 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 2098 2106 2003 2011 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 2216 2218 2117 2119 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B20">20</xref>
###xml 2219 2221 2120 2122 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B41">41</xref>
###xml 2222 2224 2123 2125 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B42">42</xref>
###xml 733 740 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Based on a crystal structure of residues 1-140 of delta in complex with a monomeric form of the beta clamp betamonomer, residues V36, L177, P242, V247 and M362 of the clamp interact directly with M71, L73 and P74 of delta (39). Furthermore, a separate study reported that substitution of residues P363, M364 or L366 in beta with Ala impaired interactions of the clamp with delta (33). Based on these results, we hypothesized that deletion of the C-terminal five residues (M362-L366) of the clamp would impair the ability of the cleft to interact with the CBM present in most clamp partner proteins (Figure 1A). We will refer to this beta cleft mutant as betaC. In silico modeling of betaC using the PDB coordinates for the wild-type E. coli beta clamp (1MMI) and the Insight II software suggested that deletion of residues M362-L366 not only removed residues contributing to the cleft region, but additionally caused the cleft to partially collapse in upon itself, rendering it unable to efficiently interact with the CBM, without affecting the tertiary structure of the clamp or its ability to dimerize in solution. Consistent with our in silico modeling, purified betaC chromatographed as a dimer in gel filtration (Figure 1C and D), and was indistinguishable from beta+ by circular dichroism spectroscopy (Figure 1B), indicating that the wild-type and betaC clamps contained comparable fractions of alpha-helix, beta-sheet and beta-turn elements. Furthermore, betaC failed to interact with the delta subunit of the DnaX complex (Figure 1C), indicating that the cleft was severely impaired for interacting with the CBM of delta. In contrast, beta+ interacted with delta, forming what appeared to be a mixture of complexes differing in their stoichiometries of beta+ and delta, or the structures of beta+ and/or delta within the complex(es), resulting in an altered mobility. These findings are consistent with a previous report concluding that as many as two delta subunits could bind a single clamp in solution (40). The betaC clamp was also severely impaired for interaction with Pol IIIalpha (Figure 1D), consistent with previous reports concluding that the CBM of Pol IIIalpha contacts the cleft of the clamp (20,41,42). Based on these findings, we conclude that deletion of residues M362-L366 severely impairs the cleft region of the clamp, abrogating its ability to interact with the CBM, without significantly affecting the overall tertiary structure of the clamp.
###end p 39
###begin title 40
###xml 86 87 80 81 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 102 103 93 94 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 108 109 96 97 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
Purification of a heterodimeric beta clamp bearing one wild-type protomer and one betaC protomer (beta+/betaC)
###end title 40
###begin p 41
###xml 186 187 183 184 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 192 193 186 187 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 251 252 242 243 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 260 261 251 252 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sub>
###xml 273 274 261 262 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 320 327 308 315 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 346 347 331 332 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 352 353 334 335 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 409 410 388 389 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 418 419 397 398 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sub>
###xml 431 432 407 408 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 580 581 553 554 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 585 586 558 559 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sub>
###xml 598 599 568 569 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 691 699 661 669 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 855 856 825 826 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sub>
###xml 972 973 942 943 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sub>
###xml 1066 1067 1036 1037 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sub>
###xml 1083 1091 1053 1061 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 1376 1377 1346 1347 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sub>
###xml 1532 1540 1502 1510 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 1778 1786 1748 1756 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 1971 1979 1941 1949 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 2082 2083 2049 2050 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 2091 2099 2058 2066 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 2158 2159 2125 2126 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sub>
###xml 2171 2172 2135 2136 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 2180 2188 2144 2152 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 2426 2427 2390 2391 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sub>
###xml 2587 2588 2548 2549 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 2593 2594 2551 2552 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 320 327 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
In order to determine whether one or both clefts were required for loading clamp onto DNA, processive replication and unloading clamp off of DNA, we developed a method to purify the beta+/betaC heterodimeric clamp protein. Briefly, the myc-tagged beta+ and his6-tagged betaC clamp proteins were co-expressed in the same E. coli cell, and the beta+/betaC heterodimer was purified away from both myc-tagged beta+ and his6-tagged betaC homodimers using cobalt affinity chromatography (see 'Materials and Methods' section). This same approach was also used to purify a myc-tagged beta+/his6-tagged beta+ heterodimer for use as a control in experiments discussed below as noted. As summarized in Figure 2A, three distinct peaks were observed following cobalt chromatography. Based on western blot analysis using monoclonal antibodies specific to either the his6- or myc-tags, the first peak (peak 1) contained myc-tagged homodimeric clamp, the third peak (peak 3) contained his6-tagged homodimeric clamp, and the middle peak (peak 2) contained both the myc-tagged and his6-tagged clamps (Figure 2B), suggesting that it was heterodimeric. The presence of the heterodimer in peak 2 was directly demonstrated using an SPR assay. For this assay, we covalently attached either anti-Penta*His or anti-myc antibody to the sensor chip surface. After antibody-capture of the appropriate his6- or myc-tagged clamp protein, we asked whether the second tag was present by injecting the corresponding antibody over the chip surface. As summarized in Figure 2, we were able to capture the clamp from peak 2 with either anti-Penta*His or anti-myc antibodies. Subsequent injection of the anti-myc antibody over the anti-Penta*His captured peak 2-clamp sample indicated that the myc-tag was present (Figure 2C). Similar results were observed for the reciprocal experiment in which the peak 2-clamp sample was captured using anti-myc antibody, followed by injection of anti-Penta*His antibody (Figure 2D). As controls, we verified that the anti-Penta*His antibody was unable to capture the myc-tagged beta+ clamp (Figure 2C), and the anti-myc antibody was unable to capture the his6-tagged beta+ clamp (Figure 2D). Identical results were observed using the anti-Penta*His and anti-myc antibodies in a native polyacrylamide gel electrophoretic mobility shift assay (data not shown). Taken together, these findings indicate that the myc-tagged and his6-tagged clamps present in peak 2 existed as a heterodimeric clamp. Results from additional SPR experiments discussed below further verify the purity of our beta+/betaC heterodimer preparation.
###end p 41
###begin title 42
A single dimeric beta clamp simultaneously binds two delta subunits
###end title 42
###begin p 43
###xml 63 65 56 58 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B20">20</xref>
###xml 66 68 59 61 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B39">39</xref>
###xml 246 248 235 237 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B40">40</xref>
###xml 259 267 248 256 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 298 299 284 285 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 304 305 287 288 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 547 548 519 520 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 554 555 523 524 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 564 565 530 531 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 570 571 533 534 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 649 650 612 613 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">R</italic>
###xml 650 653 613 616 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">max</sub>
Residues L73-F74 of delta contact the cleft on the beta clamp (20,39). Since the clamp has two clefts, we hypothesized that it could simultaneously interact with two delta subunits. Results of gel filtration experiments support this hypothesis [(40); and see Figure 1C]. In contrast, since the beta+/betaC heterodimer has only one functional cleft, we hypothesized that it would interact with only a single delta. As a direct test of these hypotheses, we used an SPR assay similar to that discussed above to analyze interactions of delta with beta+, betaC and beta+/betaC. Of relevance to these experiments, the magnitude of the maximal SPR signal (Rmax) is directly proportional to molecular weight of the interacting partner. Thus, the stoichiometry of interacting partners within a complex can be determined.
###end p 43
###begin p 44
###xml 17 25 17 25 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 32 33 29 30 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 42 43 36 37 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 48 49 39 40 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 88 89 72 73 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 319 320 280 281 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">R</italic>
###xml 320 323 281 284 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">max</sub>
###xml 352 353 313 314 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">R</italic>
###xml 353 356 314 317 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">max</sub>
###xml 447 448 404 405 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">R</italic>
###xml 448 451 405 408 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">max</sub>
###xml 474 475 431 432 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">R</italic>
###xml 475 478 432 435 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">max</sub>
###xml 581 589 522 530 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 647 648 581 582 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 727 728 661 662 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sub>
###xml 748 749 679 680 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 755 756 683 684 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 776 777 701 702 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 835 836 760 761 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sub>
###xml 857 858 779 780 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 863 864 782 783 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 867 875 786 794 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 973 974 889 890 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 979 980 892 893 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1283 1284 1180 1181 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sub>
As summarized in Figure 3A, beta+ and beta+/betaC each interacted with delta, while betaC failed to do so. For these experiments, we captured approximately100 RU of each clamp on the chip surface. The beta clamp is 81.2 kDa as dimer, and delta is 38.7 kDa. Thus, if one delta interacted with the clamp, the theoretical Rmax would be 48 RU [theoretical Rmax = (100 RU) x (38.7 kDa/81.2 kDa) x 1], while binding of two delta subunits would yield an Rmax of 96 RU [theoretical Rmax = (100 RU) x (38.7 kDa/81.2 kDa)x2]. The binding response for delta saturated at approximately100 RU (Figure 3A), indicating that two delta subunits bound a single beta+ clamp. Identical results were obtained regardless of whether we utilized a his6-tagged form of beta+ (beta+), or a form of beta+ comprised of one myc-tagged subunit in complex with a his6-tagged subunit (beta+/beta+) (Figure 3A). Importantly, since this clamp was captured using anti-Penta*His antibody, the result with beta+/beta+ indicates that upon binding two delta subunits, the clamp persists as a dimer in solution. If each delta bound to a separate cleft, and binding of each delta acted to open a dimer interface, binding of two delta subunits would have broken the clamp dimer, releasing the myc-tagged protomer from the his6-tagged beta subunit captured on the chip surface, reducing the RU signal.
###end p 44
###begin p 45
###xml 54 55 47 48 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 60 61 50 51 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 88 96 78 86 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 194 195 153 154 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 200 201 156 157 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 277 278 233 234 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">R</italic>
###xml 278 281 234 237 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">max</sub>
###xml 361 362 314 315 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 367 368 317 318 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 449 450 392 393 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 455 456 395 396 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
We next determined the stoichiometry of the delta-beta+/betaC complex. As summarized in Figure 3A, the binding response for delta saturated at approximately50 RU when approximately100 RU of beta+/betaC was captured on the chip surface. This value is similar to the theoretical Rmax limit of 48 RU for 1:1 binding under these conditions, indicating that the beta+/betaC heterodimer bound a single delta subunit. This result demonstrates that our beta+/betaC preparation is homogeneous.
###end p 45
###begin title 46
Two delta subunits interact cooperatively with a single beta clamp
###end title 46
###begin p 47
###xml 159 160 152 153 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 179 180 165 166 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 185 186 168 169 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 255 256 234 235 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 256 257 235 236 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D</sub>
###xml 291 299 270 278 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 342 343 318 319 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 348 349 321 322 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 403 404 370 371 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sup>
###xml 422 423 386 387 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 447 448 405 406 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sup>
###xml 526 527 484 485 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 527 528 485 486 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D</sub>
###xml 592 593 547 548 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 730 731 678 679 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 914 922 854 862 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 1005 1007 937 939 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;3</sup>
###xml 1009 1011 941 943 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;1</sup>
###xml 1105 1107 1033 1035 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;2</sup>
###xml 1109 1111 1037 1039 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;1</sup>
###xml 1135 1136 1063 1064 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 1136 1137 1064 1065 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D</sub>
###xml 1146 1147 1071 1072 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1384 1385 1297 1298 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 1385 1386 1298 1299 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D</sub>
###xml 1399 1407 1312 1320 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 1452 1453 1365 1366 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 1453 1454 1366 1367 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D</sub>
###xml 1484 1485 1394 1395 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1490 1491 1397 1398 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 1581 1582 1482 1483 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sup>
###xml 1643 1644 1541 1542 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1649 1650 1544 1545 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 1717 1718 1605 1606 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1818 1819 1699 1700 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 1891 1892 1769 1770 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1897 1898 1772 1773 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
In addition to analyzing stoichiometries, we were also interested in determining kinetic constants for each clamp-delta interaction. Attempts to model the beta+-delta and the beta+/betaC-delta interactions as simple 1:1 (Langmuir) associations revealed a KD of 43 and 15.6 nM, respectively (Figure 3B, D and F). Although the data for the beta+/betaC-delta interaction fit well to the Langmuir model (chi2 = 9.38), the beta+-delta data did not (chi2 = 129), suggesting that it was not a simple 1:1 interaction. Thus, the 43 nM KD value based on Langmuir binding inaccurately describes the beta+-delta interaction. Closer inspection of the shapes of the association and dissociation phases of the sensorgrams suggested that the beta+-delta interaction involved negative cooperativity. For example, the shape of the dissociation phase of the sensorgram changed significantly as a function of the delta concentration (Figure 3C). At low delta concentrations (<50 nM), dissociation of delta was slow (2.22 x 10-3 s-1), while at high delta concentrations (>50 nM) its dissociation was 5.3-fold faster (1.17 x 10-2 s-1). Recalculation of the KD for beta+-delta utilizing only the sensorgrams resulting from lower concentrations of delta (0.1-50 nM) using the Langmuir binding model, under the assumption that these results largely reflect binding of the first delta to the clamp, revealed a KD of 17.5 nM (Figure 3B and F), which is very close to the 15.6 nM KD value calculated for the beta+/betaC-delta heterodimer. Furthermore, this data set fit well to the Langmuir binding model (chi2 = 3.25). Taken together, these results suggest that the beta+/betaC heterodimer is fully proficient for binding one delta via the beta+ subunit, but is unable to bind the second delta due to the mutation affecting the cleft in the betaC subunit. These findings also further demonstrate the purity of our beta+/betaC preparation.
###end p 47

###xml 2124 2627 1956 2449 <fig xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="F4" position="float"><label>Figure 4.</label><caption><p textid="49">Analysis of the &#946;<sup>+</sup>&#8211;&#948; interaction using isothermal titration calorimetery (ITC). In order to further characterize interactions of beta+ with delta, we took advantage of the fact that dissociation of delta from the clamp was biphasic (Figure 3B and C). Since only the slow dissociation phase (2.22 x 10-3 s-1) was observed when low levels of delta were injected, it must result from loss of the tightly bound delta, while the rapid phase (1.17 x 10-2 s-1) reflects dissociation of the second, more loosely bound delta. As a result of this binding mechanism, we were able to perform a 'double-injection' experiment (see Figure 3E), in which we first injected a saturating level of delta over captured beta+ to form a beta+-delta2 complex, allowed for dissociation of the more loosely bound delta (delta2), resulting in a beta+-delta1 complex, and then injected increasing levels of delta over the beta+-delta1 complex to characterize binding of the second delta (delta2) to the clamp. Using this approach, delta2 bound the beta+-delta1 complex with a KD of 160 nM (chi2 = 1.43), or roughly 10-fold less tightly than our estimated KD for binding of the first delta (KDdelta1 = 17.5 nM; see Figure 3E and F). To confirm that our double inject experiment accurately measured the affinity of the beta2-delta1 complex for delta2 we also characterized this interaction using ITC. ITC isotherms fit well to the sequential binding sites model (Figure 4), yielding KD values for binding of the two delta subunits of 259 nM and 4 muM, respectively. The approximately15-fold different in KD values calculated by ITC is similar to the approximately10-fold difference observed by SPR (Figure 3F). The KD values determined by ITC are weaker than those determined by SPR because the SPR experiments were performed at 25degreesC, while the ITC was performed at 37degreesC, and KA decreases as temperature increases. Nevertheless, these findings indicate that two delta subunits simultaneously bind a single beta clamp with negative cooperativity. Finally, the intracellular concentration of delta is reported to be approximately1.4 muM (32). Thus, the observed negative cooperativity is likely to be biologically relevant. Figure 4.Analysis of the beta+-delta interaction using isothermal titration calorimetery (ITC). ITC analysis was performed as described in 'Materials and Methods' section. The top panel shows heat changes associated with each injection of beta+ clamp. The bottom panel shows the fit of the integrated heats to the sequential binding sites model. KD values were calculated by taking the reciprocal of K1 (3.86 x 106) and K2 (2.50 x 105) derived from the fit to the sequential binding sites model (inset).
###end p 48

###xml 532 533 506 507 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>

###xml 2410 2410 2247 2247 <graphic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xlink:href="gkp128f5"/>
###xml 1236 2410 1169 2247 <fig xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="F5" position="float"><label>Figure 5.</label><caption><p textid="52">Interactions of wild-type and mutant clamps with the DnaX complex. (<bold>A</bold>) Representative SPR results analyzing interaction of DnaX (100 nM) with various &#946; clamp proteins (&#8764;100 RU). (<bold>B</bold>) Titration of DnaX with &#946;<sup>+</sup>. Increasing concentrations of the DnaX complex (0, 1, 10, 50, 100, 200 and 500 nM) were injected over &#8764;100 RU of his<sub>6</sub>-tagged &#946;<sup>+</sup> captured on the anti-Penta&#8226;His chip surface. (<bold>C</bold>) Titration of DnaX with &#946;<sup>+</sup>/&#946;<sup>C</sup>. Increasing concentrations of the DnaX complex [1 (in duplicate), 10, 50, 100, 500 (in duplicate) and 1000 nM] were injected over &#8764;100 RU of &#946;<sup>+</sup>/&#946;<sup>C</sup> captured on the anti-Penta&#8226;His chip surface. (<bold>D</bold>) Summary table of kinetic constants for various clamp&#8211;DnaX interactions derived from SPR results summarized in (B) and (C). The <italic>K</italic><sub>D</sub> for the DnaX&#8211;&#946;<sup>+</sup> interaction was reported previously (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="B11">11</xref>), and is included here for direct comparison to &#946;<sup>C</sup> and &#946;<sup>+</sup>/&#946;<sup>C</sup>. An interaction of &#946;<sup>C</sup> with DnaX was not detected (nd) by SPR.</p></caption><graphic xlink:href="gkp128f5"/></fig>
Although DnaX is thought to contact a single cleft in the dimeric clamp (12), Pol IIIalpha contains two CBMs (41,42), and may therefore simultaneously contact both clefts. As a direct test of these hypotheses, we asked whether the beta+/betaC heterodimer interacted normally with DnaX and/or Pol IIIalpha using the same SPR assay discussed above. As summarized in Figure 5, both beta+ and beta+/betaC interacted with DnaX, while betaC failed to do so (Figure 5A). Analysis of the RU signals under steady-state conditions revealed a KD of 27 nM for beta+, and 58 nM for beta+/betaC (Figure 5B-D). The on rates of 7.84 x 106 M-1 s-1 for beta+ and 6.92 x 106 M-1 s-1 for beta+/betaC were almost identical. The only significant difference in the interactions of DnaX with the two clamps was that the off rate of DnaX from beta+/betaC was twice as fast as that observed for beta+ (Figure 5D). This 2-fold difference may be due to the fact that beta+/betaC has one-half the number of delta binding sites (i.e. clefts). Alternatively, other DnaX subunits in addition to delta may contact the second cleft. Nonetheless, these findings demonstrate that a single cleft is sufficient to support normal interaction of the clamp with DnaX in vitro. Figure 5.Interactions of wild-type and mutant clamps with the DnaX complex. (A) Representative SPR results analyzing interaction of DnaX (100 nM) with various beta clamp proteins (approximately100 RU). Clamps examined include the his6-tagged beta+ homodimer (beta+), the his6-tagged betaC homodimer (betaC) and the his6-tagged beta+/myc-tagged betaC heterodimer (beta+/betaC). (B) Titration of DnaX with beta+. Increasing concentrations of the DnaX complex (0, 1, 10, 50, 100, 200 and 500 nM) were injected over approximately100 RU of his6-tagged beta+ captured on the anti-Penta*His chip surface. (C) Titration of DnaX with beta+/betaC. Increasing concentrations of the DnaX complex [1 (in duplicate), 10, 50, 100, 500 (in duplicate) and 1000 nM] were injected over approximately100 RU of beta+/betaC captured on the anti-Penta*His chip surface. (D) Summary table of kinetic constants for various clamp-DnaX interactions derived from SPR results summarized in (B) and (C). The KD for the DnaX-beta+ interaction was reported previously (11), and is included here for direct comparison to betaC and beta+/betaC. An interaction of betaC with DnaX was not detected (nd) by SPR.
###end p 51

###xml 1298 1927 1191 1753 <fig xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="F6" position="float"><label>Figure 6.</label><caption><p textid="54">Interactions of wild-type and mutant clamps with Pol III&#945;. (<bold>B</bold>) Summary table of kinetic constants for various clamp&#8211;Pol III&#945; interactions derived from SPR experiments in which &#8764;100 RU of clamp was captured on the chip surface, and 10, 50, 100, 250, 500 and 1000 nM Pol III&#945; was injected.</p></caption><graphic xlink:href="gkp128f6"/></fig>
We next examined interactions of beta+, betaC and beta+/betaC with Pol IIIalpha. In contrast to DnaX, all three forms of the clamp interacted with Pol IIIalpha, albeit with different affinities (Figure 6). With approximately100 RU of beta+ captured on the chip surface, the binding response for Pol IIIalpha saturated at an Rmax of approximately150 RU. This is very close to the theoretical Rmax of 160 RU calculated for a 1:1 interaction, indicating that a single Pol IIIalpha was bound to the beta+ clamp. Analysis of the SPR results indicated a KD value of 108 nM (chi2 = 4.15; Figure 6B), which is consistent with previously reported values for the beta-alpha interaction (33,43). The KD for the betaC-alpha interaction was 1.78 muM (chi2 = 7.28) (Figure 6B). Since the cleft is impaired in betaC, this KD most likely represents contacts of Pol IIIalpha with noncleft surfaces of the clamp. The off rate of 4.23 x 10-3 s-1 for betaC was similar to that of beta+ (7.26 x 10-3 s-1), demonstrating that the contact(s) limiting dissociation of alpha remained intact in betaC (Figure 6B). In contrast, the on rate of 2.38 x 103 M-1 s-1 for betaC was 28-fold slower than that of beta+ (6.75 x 104 M-1 s-1), indicating that the cleft represents the primary contact site on the clamp for Pol IIIalpha. Figure 6.Interactions of wild-type and mutant clamps with Pol IIIalpha. (A) Representative SPR results analyzing interaction of Pol IIIalpha (500 nM) with various beta clamp proteins (approximately100 RU). Clamps examined include the his6-tagged beta+ homodimer (beta+), the his6-tagged betaC homodimer (betaC) and the his6-tagged beta+/myc-tagged betaC heterodimer (beta+/betaC). (B) Summary table of kinetic constants for various clamp-Pol IIIalpha interactions derived from SPR experiments in which approximately100 RU of clamp was captured on the chip surface, and 10, 50, 100, 250, 500 and 1000 nM Pol IIIalpha was injected.
###end p 53

###begin p 55
###xml 4 5 4 5 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 5 6 5 6 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D</sub>
###xml 35 36 28 29 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 41 42 31 32 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 70 71 58 59 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sup>
###xml 109 110 97 98 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sup>
###xml 112 114 100 102 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;1</sup>
###xml 116 118 104 106 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;1</sup>
###xml 171 172 156 157 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 174 182 159 167 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 256 257 234 235 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 281 282 256 257 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 287 288 259 260 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 328 330 300 302 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;3</sup>
###xml 332 334 304 306 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;1</sup>
###xml 381 382 350 351 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
The KD of Pol IIIalpha for the beta+/betaC heterodimer was 172 nM (chi2 = 3.03), with an on rate of 7.27 x 104 M-1 s-1. These values are similar to those observed for beta+ (Figure 6B), suggesting that Pol IIIalpha is bound to the cleft present on the beta+ subunit within the beta+/betaC heterodimer. The off rate was 12.5 x 10-3 s-1, which is comparable to that observed for beta+. These results, taken together with those discussed above, demonstrate unambiguously that a single cleft is sufficient to support normal interaction of the clamp with both DnaX and Pol IIIalpha.
###end p 55
###begin title 56
Only one cleft is required for clamp loading, while both clefts contribute to its unloading
###end title 56
###begin p 57
###xml 53 55 41 43 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B32">32</xref>
###xml 56 58 44 46 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B35">35</xref>
###xml 128 130 113 115 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B32">32</xref>
###xml 531 533 488 490 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B32">32</xref>
###xml 616 624 573 581 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
There are only approximately300-600 clamps per cell (32,35), and once loaded, beta remains on DNA with a half-life of >100 min (32). Since there are approximately4000 Okazaki fragments synthesized on lagging strand during each replication cycle, it is necessary that clamps be recycled approximately10 times each. This recycling presumably involves their active removal from DNA, returning them to the soluble pool that supplies clamps for lagging strand replication. DnaX and delta can each catalyze unloading of clamps from DNA (32). We therefore asked whether one or both clefts were required for clamp unloading in vitro.
###end p 57
###begin p 58
###xml 121 122 118 119 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sub>
###xml 214 216 211 213 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
###xml 248 250 245 247 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B32">32</xref>
###xml 517 518 499 500 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 523 524 502 503 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 554 562 533 541 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F7">Figure 7</xref>
###xml 601 602 565 566 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 615 623 579 587 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F7">Figure 7</xref>
###xml 644 645 605 606 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 662 670 623 631 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F7">Figure 7</xref>
###xml 758 766 719 727 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">Figure 5</xref>
###xml 769 778 730 739 <label xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 7.</label>
###xml 793 794 751 752 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 800 801 755 756 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 810 811 762 763 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 816 817 765 766 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 854 855 800 801 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 857 858 803 804 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</bold>
###xml 865 866 808 809 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 868 869 811 812 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</bold>
###xml 878 879 818 819 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 884 885 821 822 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 887 888 824 825 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</bold>
###xml 995 996 929 930 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>

In order to facilitate quantitation of the level of beta clamp on and off of DNA, we took advantage of our N-terminal his6-tag, which also contains the cAMP-dependent kinase motif, to label our clamp proteins with 32P-ATP, as described previously (32). An aliquot of each loading reaction, as well as each relevant column fraction, was fractionated on a native agarose gel to separate clamp that was loaded onto nicked pBluescript plasmid DNA from free clamp. Based on densitometric analysis, approximately72% of beta+/betaC was loaded onto DNA by DnaX (Figure 7C), while only approximately46% of beta+ was loaded (Figure 7B). In contrast, betaC was not loaded (Figure 7A), consistent with our findings that this mutant protein failed to interact with DnaX (Figure 5). The myc-tagged beta+/his6-tagged beta+ protein (beta+/beta+) was used for the beta+ results shown in (B). Positions of free clamp (free beta), and clamp loaded onto nicked DNA (beta on DNA) are shown. Phosphorimager analysis displaying positions of radiolabeled clamp proteins is shown at the top of each panel, while results of ethidium bromide staining highlighting positions of nicked and supercoiled DNAs are shown at the bottom of each panel. Results from one representative experiment are shown. This experiment was repeated at least three times, and the amount of clamp loaded onto DNA or free in each experiment was determined using the Molecular Analyst software (BioRad).

###xml 2151 2151 2018 2018 <graphic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xlink:href="gkp128f8"/>
###xml 1204 2151 1122 2018 <fig xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="F8" position="float"><label>Figure 8.</label><caption><p textid="61">Ability of &#946;<sup>+</sup>, &#946;<sup>C</sup> and &#946;<sup>+</sup>/&#946;<sup>C</sup> to be unloaded from DNA by DnaX complex. The myc-tagged &#946;<sup>+</sup>/his<sub>6</sub>-tagged &#946;<sup>+</sup> protein (&#946;<sup>+</sup>/&#946;<sup>+</sup>) was used for the &#946;<sup>+</sup> results shown in (A) and (B). The ability of DnaX or delta to unload the beta+ or beta+/betaC clamps from DNA was measured using as substrate the beta+ and beta+/betaC clamp-DNA complexes purified in the experiments described in Figure 7. Similar levels of each purified clamp-DNA complex were incubated with either DnaX or delta, and clamp unloading was monitored using the native gel mobility shift assay. As summarized in Figure 8, titration of DnaX resulted in efficient unloading of beta+ from the DNA. Clamp unloading was evidenced by both the increased abundance of free clamp observed in Figure 8A, as well as the apparent increase in the level of clamp-free nicked circular DNA in Figure 8B. Unloading was dependent on ATP (Figure 8A and B, lane 7), as previously reported (32). These same conditions promoted unloading of beta+/betaC, albeit with a significantly reduced efficiency (Figure 8C and D). Whereas approximately1 microM of DnaX was sufficient to unload approximately50% of beta+ from DNA in 10 min, we were unable to achieve this level of unloading for beta+/betaC at concentrations of DnaX up to 5 muM. As with beta+, unloading of the beta+/betaC heterodimer by DnaX was ATP-dependent (Figure 8C and D, lane 7). Figure 8.Ability of beta+, betaC and beta+/betaC to be unloaded from DNA by DnaX complex. The ability of DnaX to unload beta+ (A, B) or beta+/betaC (C, D) from DNA was analyzed as described in 'Materials and Methods' section. The myc-tagged beta+/his6-tagged beta+ protein (beta+/beta+) was used for the beta+ results shown in (A) and (B). Positions of free clamp (free beta), and clamp loaded onto nicked DNA (beta on DNA) are shown. Results of both phosphorimager analysis, illustrating positions of radiolabeled clamp proteins (A, C), as well as ethidium bromide staining, highlighting positions of nicked circular, linear and supercoiled DNAs (B, D) are shown. DnaX was used at the following concentrations: lane 1, 0 nM; lane 2, 10 nM; lane 3, 100 nM; lane 4, 1 muM; lane 5, 2.5 muM; lanes 6 and 7, 5 muM. We were unable to reliably quantitate the level of beta+/betaC clamp unloading catalyzed by DnaX, due to the poor signal-to-noise ratio.
###end p 60

###xml 863 864 812 813 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
Ability of beta+, betaC and beta+/betaC to be unloaded from DNA by DnaX complex. The ability of DnaX to unload beta+ (A, B) or beta+/betaC (C, D) from DNA was analyzed as described in 'Materials and Methods' section. The myc-tagged beta+/his6-tagged beta+ protein (beta+/beta+) was used for the beta+ results shown in (A) and (B). Positions of free clamp (free beta), and clamp loaded onto nicked DNA (beta on DNA) are shown. Results of both phosphorimager analysis, illustrating positions of radiolabeled clamp proteins (A, C), as well as ethidium bromide staining, highlighting positions of nicked circular, linear and supercoiled DNAs (B, D) are shown. DnaX was used at the following concentrations: lane 1, 0 nM; lane 2, 10 nM; lane 3, 100 nM; lane 4, 1 muM; lane 5, 2.5 muM; lanes 6 and 7, 5 muM. We were unable to reliably quantitate the level of beta+/betaC clamp unloading catalyzed by DnaX, due to the poor signal-to-noise ratio.
###end p 61

The amount of clamp loaded onto DNA or free was determined using the Molecular Analyst software (BioRad). The fraction of clamp remaining on the DNA was measured by calculating the ratio of clamp on DNA/free clamp in each lane, and dividing this ratio by the ratio observed in the absence of added &#948; (lane 1).</p>

###xml 2331 2331 2185 2185 <graphic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xlink:href="gkp128f9"/>
###xml 791 2331 743 2185 <fig xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="F9" position="float"><label>Figure 9.</label><caption><p textid="63">Ability of &#946;<sup>+</sup>, &#946;<sup>C</sup> and &#946;<sup>+</sup>/&#946;<sup>C</sup> to be unloaded from DNA by the &#948; subunit of DnaX. The myc-tagged &#946;<sup>+</sup>/his<sub>6</sub>-tagged &#946;<sup>+</sup> protein (&#946;<sup>+</sup>/&#946;<sup>+</sup>) was used for the &#946;<sup>+</sup> results shown in (A) and (B). Unloading by delta was analyzed using the same assay. Consistent with one previous report (32), delta was able to efficiently unload beta+ from DNA (Figure 9A and B). Approximately 146 nM of delta was able to unload 50% of beta+ on DNA in 10 min (Figure 9E). This value is remarkably similar to the KD value of 160 nM describing the binding of the second delta to the beta clamp as measured by SPR (Figure 3). In contrast, delta was unable to unload the beta+/betaC heterodimer when added at concentrations up to 10 muM (Figure 9C-E). Disappearance of DNA in the presence of higher concentrations of delta was due to delta-DNA interactions (Figure 9B and D). Taken together, these findings indicate that both DnaX and delta require both clefts in order to efficiently unload clamp from DNA. Figure 9.Ability of beta+, betaC and beta+/betaC to be unloaded from DNA by the delta subunit of DnaX. The ability of delta to unload beta+ (A, B) or beta+/betaC (C, D) from DNA was analyzed as described in 'Materials and Methods' section. The myc-tagged beta+/his6-tagged beta+ protein (beta+/beta+) was used for the beta+ results shown in (A) and (B). Positions of free clamp (free beta), and clamp loaded onto nicked DNA (beta on DNA) are shown. Results of both phosphorimager analysis, illustrating positions of radiolabeled clamp proteins (A, C), as well as ethidium bromide staining, highlighting positions of nicked circular, linear and supercoiled DNAs (B, D) are shown. For beta+/beta+, delta was used at the following concentrations: lane 1, 0 nM; lane 2, 15 nM; lane 3, 150 nM; lane 4, 300 nM; lane 5, 450 nM; lane 6, 750 nM; lane 7, 1050 nM; lane 8, 1.2 muM; lane 9, 1.5 muM; lane 10, 2.5 muM; lane 11, 5 muM; lane 12, 10 muM. For beta+/betaC, delta was used at the following concentrations: lane 1, 0 nM; lane 2, 150 nM; lane 3, 750 nM; lane 4, 1.5 muM; lane 5, 5 muM; lane 6, 10 muM. (E) Quantitation of the results from (A) and (C) summarizing the ability of delta to unload beta+/beta+ or beta+/betaC from DNA. The amount of clamp loaded onto DNA or free was determined using the Molecular Analyst software (BioRad). The fraction of clamp remaining on the DNA was measured by calculating the ratio of clamp on DNA/free clamp in each lane, and dividing this ratio by the ratio observed in the absence of added delta (lane 1).
###end p 62

###begin title 64
###xml 4 5 1 2 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 10 11 4 5 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 63 71 57 65 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
beta+/betaC is proficient for stimulating Pol III* replication in vitro
###end title 64
###begin p 65
###xml 37 38 34 35 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 43 44 37 38 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 229 237 219 227 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 440 449 426 435 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F10">Figure 10</xref>
###xml 550 551 533 534 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 598 607 581 590 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F10">Figure 10</xref>
###xml 762 763 738 739 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 771 772 744 745 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 777 778 747 748 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 831 840 801 810 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F10">Figure 10</xref>
###xml 951 959 921 929 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 961 971 931 941 <label xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 10.</label>
###xml 986 987 953 954 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 993 994 957 958 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 1004 1005 965 966 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1010 1011 968 969 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</sup>
###xml 1046 1054 1004 1012 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 1146 1147 1104 1105 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sub>
###xml 1159 1160 1114 1115 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1176 1177 1128 1129 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1190 1191 1139 1140 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1230 1231 1176 1177 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1236 1237 1179 1180 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 971 1354 941 1297 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="66">Ability of &#946;<sup>+</sup>, &#946;<sup>C</sup>, and &#946;<sup>+</sup>/&#946;<sup>C</sup> to stimulate Pol III* replication <italic>in vitro</italic>. The his<sub>6</sub>-tagged &#946;<sup>+</sup>/myc-tagged &#946;<sup>+</sup> form of &#946;<sup>+</sup> was used as the positive control (&#946;<sup>+</sup>/&#946;<sup>+</sup>). Results shown represent the average of three separate determinations. Error bars represent the standard deviation.</p>
###xml 971 1354 941 1297 <caption xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><p textid="66">Ability of &#946;<sup>+</sup>, &#946;<sup>C</sup>, and &#946;<sup>+</sup>/&#946;<sup>C</sup> to stimulate Pol III* replication <italic>in vitro</italic>.
